All Souls Equal in Essence? Instrument Theory
Razi reports ancient philosophers' view on soul equality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ancient philosophical view that all souls (human and animal) are identical in essence and that observed differences in cognition and action arise solely from bodily instruments.

Core Idea
Souls are identical; bodies make the difference.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi reports an influential theory from ancient philosophy. The idea is radical: your soul is not essentially different from an animal's—what makes you think and speak is just your brain and tongue. This sets the stage for examining whether the soul's powers are innate or acquired.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own report come through.
This is a reported view, not the author's own.
2
Identify the core claim
Find the statement that all souls are equal in complete essence (تمام الماهية). This is the central idea.
3
Examine the two hypotheticals
The passage gives two conditional examples: brain and tongue. Notice how each illustrates that equal instruments would produce equal powers.
The examples are meant to show that essence alone does not cause differences.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider: if this view is true, what does it say about the soul-body relationship? Is the soul merely a function of the body?
This view contrasts with other philosophical and theological positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب جمع عظيم من قدماء الفلاسفة : إلى أن النفوس الإنسانية والحيوانية : متساوية في تمام الماهية ، وأن اختلاف أفعالها وإدراكاتها إنما حصل بسبب اختلاف آلاتها وأدواتها ، فلو كان دماغ سائر الحيوانات مساوياً لدماغ الإنسان ، لكانت نفوس سائر الحيوانات مساوية للنفوس الإنسانية في التعقلات والتفكرات ، ولو كان لسان سائر الحيوانات ، مساوياً للسان الإنسان. لكان مساوياً له في قوة النطق .
A great multitude of the ancient philosophers held that human and animal souls are equal in complete essence, and that the difference in their actions and perceptions only occurs due to the difference in their instruments and tools. So if the brain of all animals were equal to the human brain, then the souls of all animals would be equal to human souls in intellections and thoughts, and if the tongue of all animals were equal to the human tongue, it would be equal to it in the power of speech.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage reports the view of a group of ancient philosophers. They claim that all souls (human and animal) are identical in their essential nature (al-mahiyya). The observed differences in actions and perceptions are entirely due to the differences in bodily instruments (ālāt wa adawāt). They illustrate with two hypotheticals: if animals had a brain equal to humans, they would reason; if they had a tongue equal to humans, they would speak. This emphasizes that essence is one, but bodily tools cause variation.

Key Terms
النفوس
الماهية
الآلات
التعقلات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that this passage presents the author's (al-Razi's) own view.
Correction: The passage explicitly attributes the view to 'a great multitude of the ancient philosophers' (ذهب جمع عظيم من قدماء الفلاسفة). It is a report, not an endorsement.

Checkpoint
According to the ancient philosophers reported here, what is the cause of the difference in actions between human and animal souls?
A) Difference in essence
B) Difference in bodily instruments
C) Difference in the power of speech
D) Difference in brain size

Key Takeaway
The ancient philosophers argued that soul essence is uniform, and variation in mental abilities is due solely to bodily instruments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If souls are equal in essence, what does that say about your own potential? Do you use the instruments you have (mind, tongue) to their fullest, or do you blame your 'essence' for shortcomings?
?
Consider the hypothetical: if you had been born with a different brain or tongue, would you be a different person? How does this view affect your sense of personal responsibility?
?
How does the claim that all souls are equal challenge the way you treat others? Do you see the differences in abilities as merely instrumental, or do you judge people's essence?

Ibn Sina on Human Souls: Immaterial but Varied by Temperament
Ibn Sina's view on human souls and the role of temperament.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's view that human rational souls are immaterial and equal in essence, and that individual differences in intellect and character arise from bodily temperaments.

Core Idea
Human souls are equal in essence; differences come from the body, not the soul itself.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents the view of Ibn Sina (Avicenna) on the nature of human souls. Ibn Sina distinguishes sharply between animal souls (which are physical) and human rational souls (which are immaterial). Yet despite their immateriality, all human souls are identical in essence. To explain the observable differences in intelligence and morality among people, Ibn Sina turns to the body: variations in temperament cause the apparent differences. This lesson unpacks Ibn Sina's argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn Sina's claims
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of Ibn Sina's argument. Pay attention to his initial distinction between animal and human souls, and then his claim of equality followed by an explanation of differences.
Notice the two key moves: first a distinction, then a surprising claim of equality.
2
Understand the soul distinction
Identify what Ibn Sina says about animal souls (physical powers) versus human rational souls (immaterial substances). This is the foundation of his view.
The term 'جواهر مجردة' (immaterial substances) is crucial for human souls.
3
Explore the role of temperament
See how Ibn Sina uses bodily temperaments to explain differences observed among humans. He gives examples of choleric and phlegmatic temperaments. Reflect on why temperaments being infinite leads to infinite differences in souls' powers.
This move preserves the essential unity of souls while accounting for diversity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشيخ الرئيس أبو علي بن سينا : فإنه زعم أن نفوس سائر الحيوانات قوى جسمانية ، وليست جواهر مجردة . وأما النفوس الناطقة البشرية فإنها جواهر مجردة في ذواتها . ثم زعم : أنها بأسرها متساوية في تمام الماهية والحقيقة ، ولما شاهدنا اختلاف الناس في الذكاء والبلادة ، والأخلاق الفاضلة والمذمومة . زعم : أن ذلك الاختلاف إنما حصل بسبب اختلاف الأمزجة البدنية . فمن كان صفراوي المزاج ، كان الفرح وحسن الاخلاق غالباً عليه . ومن كان بلغمي المزاج ، كانت آثاره شبيهة بأحوال السوداء . ولما ثبت في باب المزاج : أن مراتب الأمزجة مختلفة ، وغير متناهية ، لا كانت مراتب اختلاف النفوس في قوة الإدراك وقوة الحركة غير متناهية .
As for the Chief Master Abu Ali ibn Sina, he claimed that the souls of all animals are physical powers and not immaterial substances. As for the human rational souls, they are immaterial substances in their essences. Then he claimed that they are all equal in complete essence and reality. And when we observe the difference among people in intelligence and dullness, and virtuous and blameworthy morals, he claimed that this difference only occurs due to the difference in bodily temperaments. So whoever has a choleric temperament, joy and good morals prevail over him. And whoever has a phlegmatic temperament, his effects resemble the states of black bile. And since it is established in the chapter on temperament that the levels of temperaments are different and infinite, so the levels of difference of souls in the power of perception and the power of motion are infinite.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Sina's view. He distinguishes between animal souls (physical powers) and human rational souls (immaterial substances). Despite the immateriality of human souls, they are all equal in essence. The observed variations in intelligence, morality, and character are attributed to differences in bodily temperaments (amzija badaniyya). He gives examples: a choleric temperament leads to joy and good morals; a phlegmatic temperament leads to effects resembling black bile (melancholy). Since temperaments vary infinitely, the differences in souls' powers of perception and motion are also infinite. Thus, Ibn Sina preserves the essential unity of human souls while accounting for diversity through bodily causes.

Key Terms
النفوس الناطقة
جواهر مجردة
الأمزجة البدنية
الصفراوي
البلغمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that differences in intelligence and morals are due to differences in the souls themselves.
Correction: Ibn Sina holds that human souls are equal in essence; all differences come from bodily temperaments.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Sina as reported here, what causes the differences in intelligence and morals among humans?
A) Difference in the essence of souls
B) Difference in bodily temperaments
C) Difference in planetary spirits
D) Difference in the power of speech

Key Takeaway
Ibn Sina maintains the essential equality of human souls while attributing all observable differences to the body's temperament.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all human souls are equal in essence, then your intelligence or dullness is not due to your soul but your body. Does this view force you to reconsider how you judge others' spiritual capacity? How can you treat someone you consider less intelligent as equally worthy of divine grace starting today?
?
Ibn Sina says differences in morality come from temperament. If your bad habits are partly due to your physical makeup, does that reduce your responsibility to improve? Or does it call you to work harder against your temperament? Write down one specific moral weakness you have blamed on your nature and commit to one practical step to overcome it this week.
?
The passage implies your soul is not inherently better than any other. How does that challenge your pride in your own intellect or character? When have you felt superior to someone because of your knowledge or morals? What concrete action can you take today to humble yourself and serve that person?

The Third View: Human Souls as Species from Planetary Spirits
Razi expounds the view that human souls are species under a genus, each species sourced from a planetary spirit called al-tiba' al-tamm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ancient philosophical view that human souls are different species derived from planetary spirits called 'the complete nature' and how this explains human variety and affinity.

Core Idea
Every human soul belongs to a species shaped by a planetary 'father' spirit.

This passage presents a fascinating cosmological theory from ancient philosophers, as reported by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. According to this view, the human soul is not a single type but a genus containing distinct species, each originating from a specific planetary spirit. Understanding this view helps us appreciate the diversity of human dispositions and the philosophical basis for love between strangers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then its translation. Notice how Razi structures the explanation: first the general claim, then the naming of the planetary spirit, then the analogy, and finally the social implication.
This is a reported doctrine, not Razi's own view.
2
Identify the key concept: al-tiba' al-tamm
Focus on why the philosophers called the planetary spirit 'the complete nature'. The passage gives a causal reasoning: the effect must resemble its cause, so the spirit has those attributes in a more perfect form.
Think of it as the perfect source of imperfect copies.
3
Understand the father-child analogy
The passage compares the planetary spirit to a father and the souls to children. Just as a father has compassion and influence, so does the spirit nurture its species of souls.
This analogy explains how the spirit's qualities manifest in the souls.
4
Recognize the implication for human relationships
The passage ends by noting that souls of the same species share a natural affinity, leading to inexplicable love between strangers. This ties the cosmology to everyday experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطائفة الثالثة : زعموا : أن النفس البشرية جنس تحته أنواع مختلفة بالماهية ، وتحت كل نوع أشخاص متساوية بالماهية ، وكل نوع من تلك الأنواع ، فهو كالنتيجة من روح معين من أرواح الكواكب ، فنوع منها حرة كريمة فاضلة ، قوية في الفهم والأفعال الجميلة ، ونوع آخر منها نذلة شريرة بليدة . وذلك الروح الكوكبي الذي هو المبدأ لذلك النوع ، هو المسمى في اصطلاحات قدماء الفلاسفة : بالطباع التام . وإنما سموه بهذا الإسم ، لأن المعلول لا بد وأن يكون من جنس العلة . وشبيهاً بها . فكل صفة وخصلة ، حصلت لذلك النوع المعين من النفوس البشرية ، فهي إنما حصلت بتأثير ذلك الروح الفلكي ، ولا شك أن تلك الخواص والصفات في ذلك الروح الفلكي أكمل منها في تلك النفوس . فلهذا السبب سموا تلك الأصول بالطباع التام . وهذه النفوس كالأولاد لذلك الروح ، وهو كالأب لهذه النفوس . وكما أن الأب له شفقة ومحبة على أولاده، فكذلك لذلك الروح مزيد معونة في تربية ذلك النوع من النفوس . فإن كان ذلك الطباع التام من الأرواح الفاضلة الكريمة الخيرة العاقلة ، ظهرت تلك الآثار في هذه النفوس . وإن كانت بالضد كان أحوال تلك النفوس على وفق أحوال ذلك الأب . وأيضاً : فتلك النفوس لما كانت من نوع واحد ، لا جرم حصل بينها نوع مجانسة ومشاكلة ، وحصل بينها لهذا السبب مزيد محبة ومودة . ولهذا السبب قد يتفق بين شخصين أجنبيين من المحبة ما لا يزاد عليها .
And the third group claimed that the human soul is a genus under which are different species in essence, and under each species are individuals equal in essence. Each of those species is like the result from a specific spirit among the planetary spirits. So one species is free, generous, virtuous, strong in understanding and beautiful actions, and another species is base, evil, and dull. That planetary spirit which is the principle for that species is called in the terminologies of the ancient philosophers 'the complete nature' (al-tiba' al-tamm). They only named it with this name because the effect must necessarily be of the same kind as the cause and similar to it. So every attribute and trait that occurs to that specific species of human souls only occurs through the influence of that celestial spirit, and there is no doubt that those properties and attributes in that celestial spirit are more perfect than they are in those souls. For this reason they called those principles 'the complete nature'. And these souls are like children to that spirit, and it is like a father to these souls. Just as the father has compassion and love for his children, so that spirit has additional assistance in nurturing that species of souls. If that complete nature is among the virtuous, generous, good, rational spirits, then those effects appear in these souls. If it is opposite, then the states of those souls are in accordance with the states of that father. Also, since those souls are of one type, inevitably a kind of homogeneity and similarity occurs between them, and for this reason increased love and affection occurs between them. For this reason, sometimes between two strangers there occurs love that cannot be exceeded.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents the view of a third group of philosophers. They posit that the human soul is a genus (jins) under which there are different species (anwā') that differ in essence (māhiyya). Each species is produced by a specific planetary spirit (rūḥ min arwāḥ al-kawākib). The species can be virtuous or base. That spirit is called 'the complete nature' (al-ṭiba' al-tāmm) because the effect must be similar to its cause. The spirit has the attributes in a more perfect form. These souls are like children to that spirit, which acts as a father, providing care and influence. This explains why individuals of the same species have mutual affinity and love, even between strangers.

Key Terms
الطباع التام
النفس البشرية
النوع
الروح الكوكبي
الجنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Students may think this is Razi's own cosmological view.
Correction: This is a reported doctrine of ancient philosophers; Razi is presenting it as one of several views.

Checkpoint
Why do the third group call the planetary spirit 'al-ṭiba' al-tāmm' (the complete nature)?
A) Because it has fully developed temperament
B) Because the effect must be of the same kind as its cause
C) Because it is the most perfect of all spirits
D) Because it creates souls directly

Key Takeaway
The ancient philosophers held that human souls are of different species, each derived from a planetary spirit called 'the complete nature,' which influences their qualities and affinities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believed your soul belonged to a specific species determined by a planetary spirit, would you feel less responsible for your moral failings? How does this passage challenge or affirm your own sense of personal accountability?
?
Think of a stranger you felt an inexplicable deep connection with. According to this view, it might be due to sharing the same species. Does that explanation satisfy you, or do you long for a different account of such bonds? What does your heart truly seek?
?
The ancient philosophers saw the planetary spirit as a father nurturing its souls. Do you sense any paternal care from the cosmos? If not, what does that emptiness reveal about your understanding of where your virtues come from?

The Third Group's Doctrine: Souls as Species from Planetary Spirits
Razi states the third group's doctrine of souls as types from planetary spirits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third group's claim that the human soul is a genus with species differing in quiddity, each species originating from a specific planetary spirit.

Core Idea
Human souls are like results from planetary spirits.

Razi presents the third group's doctrine, which asserts that human souls are not uniform but belong to species with distinct essences, each species emanating from a celestial spirit. This lesson introduces that foundational claim and its initial classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim
Read the first sentence carefully. Notice the structure: the human soul is a genus, with species differing in quiddity, and individuals equal in quiddity.
The term 'quiddity' means essence.
2
Identify the species origin
Each species is like a result from a specific planetary spirit. This is a key causal claim.
3
Notice the two categories
The passage divides species into two kinds: noble/virtuous and base/evil. Reflect on why this classification follows from the origin.
This sets up the later explanation of the spirit's influence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطائفة الثالثة : زعموا : أن النفس البشرية جنس تحته أنواع مختلفة بالماهية ، وتحت كل نوع أشخاص متساوية بالماهية ، وكل نوع من تلك الأنواع ، فهو كالنتيجة من روح معين من أرواح الكواكب ، فنـوع منها حرة كريمة فاضلة ، قوية في الفهم والأفعال الجميلة ، ونوع آخر منها نذلة شريرة بليدة . وذلك الروح الكوكبي الذي هو المبدأ لذلك النوع ، هو المسمى في اصطلاحات قدماء الفلاسفة : بالطباع التام . وإنما سموه بهذا الإسم ، لأن المعلول لا بد وأن يكون من جنس العلة . وشبيهاً بها . فكل صفة وخصلة ، حصلت لذلك النوع المعين من النفوس البشرية ، فهي إنما حصلت بتأثير ذلك الروح الفلكي ، ولا شك أن تلك الخواص والصفات في ذلك الروح الفلكي أكمل منها في تلك النفوس . فلهذا السبب سموا تلك الأصول (٢) بـالـطـبـاع التام . وهذه النفوس كالأولاد لذلك الروح ، وهو كالأب لهذه النفوس . وكما أن الأب له شفقة ومحبة على أولاده، فكذلك لذلك الروح مزيد معونة في تربية ذلك النوع من النفوس . فإن كان ذلك الطباع التام من الأرواح الفاضلة الكريمة الخيرة العاقلة ، ظهرت تلك الآثار في هذه النفوس . وإن كانت بالضد كان [ أحوال تلك النفوس على وفق أحوال ذلك الأب . وأيضاً : فتلك النفوس لما كانت (۳)] من نوع واحد ، لا جرم حصل بينها نوع مجانسة ومشاكلة ، وحصل بينها لهذا السبب مزيد محبة ومودة . ولهذا السبب قد يتفق بين شخصين أجنبيين من المحبة ما لا يزاد عليها . وقد يتفق بين آخرين من النفرة والبغضة ما لا يزاد عليها ، والأظهر : أن هذا المذهب هو الذي كان يذهب إليه صاحب الوحي والشريعة ، حيث قال : الأرواح جنود مجندة ، فما تعارف منها ائتلف، وما تناكر منها اختلف ، وقال أيضاً الناس معادن ، كمعادن الذهب والفضة ، وهذا [ المذهب (١) ] هو المختار عندنا
And the third group: they claimed that the human soul is a genus under which are species different in quiddity, and under each species are individuals equal in quiddity. Each of those species is like the result from a specific spirit from the spirits of the planets. Some of them are free, noble, virtuous, strong in understanding and beautiful actions; another kind is base, evil, stupid. That planetary spirit which is the principle for that species is called in the terminologies of the ancient philosophers 'the complete nature.' They named it with this name only because the effect must necessarily be of the same kind as the cause and similar to it. So every quality and attribute that obtains for that specific species of human souls comes about only by the influence of that celestial spirit. There is no doubt that those properties and qualities in that celestial spirit are more complete than in those souls. For this reason they called those principles the 'complete nature.' These souls are like children to that spirit, and it is like the father to these souls. Just as the father has compassion and love for his children, so too that spirit has increased assistance in nurturing that species of souls. If that complete nature is among the virtuous, noble, good, rational spirits, those effects appear in these souls; if it is the opposite, then the states of those souls are in accordance with the states of that father. Also, since those souls are of one type, inevitably a kind of homogeneity and similarity occurs between them, and increased love and affection occurs between them for this reason. For this reason it may happen between two unfamiliar persons a love that cannot be increased, and it may happen between others a aversion and hatred that cannot be increased. The most apparent is that this school is the one held by the possessor of revelation and law, where he said: 'Spirits are conscripted soldiers; those that know each other become intimate, and those that are unfamiliar differ.' He also said: 'People are mines like mines of gold and silver.' And this school is the chosen one with us.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents the third group's doctrine on the nature of human souls. It begins by stating their claim: the human soul is a genus with species that differ in essence (quiddity), and under each species individuals are identical in essence. Each species is like an effect produced by a specific planetary spirit. These souls are categorized as virtuous or base, depending on the planetary spirit that is their principle. The ancient philosophers call this spirit the 'complete nature' (al-taba' al-tamm) because the effect must resemble the cause; the spirit has more perfect qualities, which it imparts to the souls. The relationship is like that of a father to his children, with the spirit nurturing its species. The passage then explains the consequences: if the spirit is virtuous, the souls are virtuous; if base, the souls are base. Souls of the same type naturally have homogeneity and mutual love, sometimes exceeding expectations. The author notes that this doctrine is the one most apparently supported by the Prophet's statements about spirits being conscripted soldiers and people being mines. The author concludes that this is the preferred school for him.

Key Terms
النفس البشرية
الماهية
الأرواح الكوكبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third group, what is the relationship between a species of human souls and a planetary spirit?
A) They are identical.
B) The species is like a result from the spirit.
C) The spirit is created from the souls.
D) There is no relationship.

Key Takeaway
The third group sees human souls as a genus with species each originating from a specific planetary spirit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul belongs to a species derived from a specific planetary spirit, do you think you are born with a fixed nature—either noble or base? How does that challenge your sense of moral responsibility? What evidence from your own life shows you can choose otherwise?
?
The passage describes some souls as 'free, noble, virtuous' and others as 'base, evil, stupid'. Have you ever judged yourself or others as permanently 'that kind of person'? How does this doctrine either confirm or disturb that judgment?
?
Consider your own moments of understanding and beautiful actions versus moments of evil and stupidity. According to this view, each species is unchangeable. Does that align with your experience of struggling to improve yourself? If not, where do you find hope for change in Islamic teaching?

The Complete Nature: Why the Planetary Spirit is Called Al-Taba' al-Tamm
Razi explains the naming of the planetary spirit as 'complete nature'.

Learning Objective
You will understand the reasoning behind calling the planetary spirit the 'complete nature' and the principle of cause-effect resemblance.

Core Idea
The effect must be of the same kind and similar to its cause.

After stating the doctrine, Razi explains why the ancient philosophers called the planetary spirit the 'complete nature.' This lesson unpacks that reasoning, grounded in the causal principle that the effect resembles its cause.

Guided Path
1
Find the term 'complete nature'
Locate where the planetary spirit is called 'complete nature' (al-taba' al-tamm).
This is a technical term in ancient philosophy.
2
Understand the reasoning
Read why they call it that: the effect must be of the same kind and similar to the cause. The cause has qualities more completely.
This is a fundamental causal principle.
3
Apply the principle
Every quality in the souls comes from the spirit, and the spirit has those qualities more completely. That's why it's called 'complete nature'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the third group: they claimed that the human soul is a genus under which are species different in quiddity, and under each species are individuals equal in quiddity. Each of those species is like the result from a specific spirit from the spirits of the planets. Some of them are free, noble, virtuous, strong in understanding and beautiful actions; another kind is base, evil, stupid. That planetary spirit which is the principle for that species is called in the terminologies of the ancient philosophers 'the complete nature.' They named it with this name only because the effect must necessarily be of the same kind as the cause and similar to it. There is no doubt that those properties and qualities in that celestial spirit are more complete than in those souls. For this reason they called those principles the 'complete nature.' These souls are like children to that spirit, and it is like the father to these souls. Just as the father has compassion and love for his children, so too that spirit has increased assistance in nurturing that species of souls. If that complete nature is among the virtuous, noble, good, rational spirits, those effects appear in these souls; if it is the opposite, then the states of those souls are in accordance with the states of that father. Commentary
This passage presents the third group's doctrine on the nature of human souls. It begins by stating their claim: the human soul is a genus with species that differ in essence (quiddity), and under each species individuals are identical in essence. Each species is like an effect produced by a specific planetary spirit. These souls are categorized as virtuous or base, depending on the planetary spirit that is their principle. The ancient philosophers call this spirit the 'complete nature' (al-taba' al-tamm) because the effect must resemble the cause; the spirit has more perfect qualities, which it imparts to the souls. The relationship is like that of a father to his children, with the spirit nurturing its species. The passage then explains the consequences: if the spirit is virtuous, the souls are virtuous; if base, the souls are base. Souls of the same type naturally have homogeneity and mutual love, sometimes exceeding expectations. The author notes that this doctrine is the one most apparently supported by the Prophet's statements about spirits being conscripted soldiers and people being mines. The author concludes that this is the preferred school for him.

Key Terms
الطبع التام
المعلول
العلة
الأصول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it creates nature completely.
B) Because the effect must be similar to the cause and the cause is more complete.
C) Because it is the most perfect being.
D) Because it completes the souls.

Key Takeaway
The planetary spirit is called 'complete nature' because it is the more perfect cause from which the souls derive their qualities.

?

?
You are an effect of a more complete cause. Are you living as though your very existence points beyond yourself? What would change if you truly believed that your soul's every good quality is a borrowed perfection - and that you owe gratitude for every breath?

The Spirit as Father and the Prophetic Support
Razi develops the father-child analogy and cites hadith to support the doctrine.

Learning Objective
You will understand the analogy between the planetary spirit and a father, and how this doctrine aligns with prophetic sayings.

Core Idea
Souls are like children to their planetary spirit, and love among similar souls reflects their common origin.

Razi extends the analogy, comparing the planetary spirit to a father with love and care for its souls. He then cites prophetic hadith to support this view, concluding it as his chosen school.

Guided Path
1
Explore the father analogy
Read how the spirit is like a father to the souls, with compassion and nurturing. Note the consequence: souls resemble their spirit.
2
Understand homogeneity
Souls of the same type have homogeneity and mutual love. This explains strong bonds between strangers.
The passage gives examples of love and hatred.
3
See the prophetic support
The author cites hadith about spirits being soldiers and people being mines. These are seen as supporting the doctrine.
The author concludes this is his chosen school.

والطائفة الثالثة : زعموا : أن النفس البشرية جنس تحته أنواع مختلفة بالماهية ، وتحت كل نوع أشخاص متساوية بالماهية ، وكل نوع من تلك الأنواع ، فهو كالنتيجة من روح معين من أرواح الكواكب ، فنـوع منها حرة كريمة فاضلة ، قوية في الفهم والأفعال الجميلة ، ونوع آخر منها نذلة شريرة بليدة . وذلك الروح الكوكبي الذي هو المبدأ لذلك النوع ، هو المسمى في اصطلاحات قدماء الفلاسفة : بالطباع التام . وإنما سموه بهذا الإسم ، لأن المعلول لا بد وأن يكون من جنس العلة . وشبيهاً بها . فكل صفة وخصلة ، حصلت لذلك النوع المعين من النفوس البشرية ، فهي إنما حصلت بتأثير ذلك الروح الفلكي ، ولا شك أن تلك الخواص والصفات في ذلك الروح الفلكي أكمل منها في تلك النفوس . فلهذا السبب سموا تلك الأصول (٢) بـالـطـبـاع التام . وهذه النفوس كالأولاد لذلك الروح ، وهو كالأب لهذه النفوس . وكما أن الأب له شفقة ومحبة على أولاده، فكذلك لذلك الروح مزيد معونة في تربية ذلك النوع من النفوس . فإن كان ذلك الطباع التام من الأرواح الفاضلة الكريمة الخيرة العاقلة ، ظهرت تلك الآثار في هذه النفوس . وإن كانت بالضد كان [ أحوال تلك النفوس على وفق أحوال ذلك الأب . وأيضاً : فتلك النفوس لما كانت (۳)] من نوع واحد ، لا جرم حصل بينها نوع مجانسة ومشاكلة ، وحصل بينها لهذا السبب مزيد محبة ومودة . ولهذا السبب قد يتفق بين شخصين أجنبيين من المحبة ما لا يزاد عليها . وقد يتفق بين آخرين من النفرة والبغضة ما لا يزاد عليها ، والأظهر : أن هذا المذهب هو الذي كان يذهب إليه صاحب الوحي والشريعة ، حيث قال : الأرواح جنود مجندة ، فما تعارف منها ائتلف، وما تناكر منها اختلف ، وقال أيضاً الناس معادن ، كمعادن الذهب والفضة ، وهذا [ المذهب (١) ] هو المختار عندنا
And the third group: they claimed that the human soul is a genus under which are species different in quiddity, and under each species are individuals equal in quiddity. Each of those species is like the result from a specific spirit from the spirits of the planets. Some of them are free, noble, virtuous, strong in understanding and beautiful actions; another kind is base, evil, stupid. That planetary spirit which is the principle for that species is called in the terminologies of the ancient philosophers 'the complete nature.' They named it with this name only because the effect must necessarily be of the same kind as the cause and similar to it. So every quality and attribute that obtains for that specific species of human souls comes about only by the influence of that celestial spirit. There is no doubt that those properties and qualities in that celestial spirit are more complete than in those souls. For this reason they called those principles the 'complete nature.' These souls are like children to that spirit, and it is like the father to these souls. Just as the father has compassion and love for his children, so too that spirit has increased assistance in nurturing that species of souls. If that complete nature is among the virtuous, noble, good, rational spirits, those effects appear in these souls; if it is the opposite, then the states of those souls are in accordance with the states of that father. Also, since those souls are of one type, inevitably a kind of homogeneity and similarity occurs between them, and increased love and affection occurs between them for this reason. For this reason it may happen between two unfamiliar persons a love that cannot be increased, and it may happen between others a aversion and hatred that cannot be increased. The most apparent is that this school is the one held by the possessor of revelation and law, where he said: 'Spirits are conscripted soldiers; those that know each other become intimate, and those that are unfamiliar differ.' He also said: 'People are mines like mines of gold and silver.' And this school is the chosen one with us.

Souls Differ in Essence Despite Similar Qualities
Razi presents the fourth group's view that souls are distinct in essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth group's argument that resemblance in qualities does not entail identity in essence, and that each soul has a unique quiddity.

Core Idea
Similarity in qualities does not prove sameness in essence.

Razi now presents the fourth group's position on the nature of human souls. They agree that souls may share similarities in knowledge and character, but they argue that such resemblance is only in attributes, not in the fundamental essence. This distinction is crucial for understanding how individual souls remain distinct even when they appear alike.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the logical structure: concession (similarities exist) followed by the key distinction (qualities vs. quiddity) and then the conclusion.
Pay attention to the contrast between 'صفات' (qualities) and 'ماهية' (quiddity).
2
Identify the core argument
Locate the sentence that states the main claim: 'المشاكلة في الصفات لا تدل على المماثلة في الماهية'. Understand why this is a significant point in the debate about souls.
This is the logical pivot of the passage.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this view entails for the individuality of souls. If each soul has a unique essence, what does that mean for personal identity and moral responsibility?
This group emphasizes essential diversity over uniformity.
4
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to ensure you grasp the main point. Use the passage to verify your answer.
The answer is found directly in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطائفة الرابعة : قالوا : النفوس البشرية ، وإن كان قد يوجد فيها ما يكون بعضها أشد مشاكلة للبعض في العلوم والأخلاق ، إلا أن تلك المشابهة والمشاكلة واقعة في الصفات لكن المشاكلة في الصفات لا تدل على المماثلة في الماهية ، فكل واحد من جواهر النفوس [ البشرية (٢) ] مخالف بالماهية والذات المخصوصة لسائر النفوس ، وإن كانت متساوية في الصفات
And the fourth group: they said: Human souls, even if there may be found among them some that are more similar to others in sciences and morals, yet that similarity and resemblance occurs in qualities, but resemblance in qualities does not indicate likeness in quiddity. So each one of the essences of human souls is different in quiddity and specific essence from the rest of the souls, even if they are equal in qualities.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth group's position on the nature of human souls. They acknowledge that souls may share similarities in knowledge and character, but they argue that such resemblance is only in attributes (qualities), not in essence (quiddity). Consequently, similarity in qualities does not prove that souls are identical in their fundamental nature. Therefore, each individual soul substance has its own unique quiddity and specific essence, distinct from all others, even if they appear equal in their qualities. This view emphasizes the numerical and essential diversity of souls, opposing the idea that souls are all the same in essence.

Key Terms

الصفات (qualities)
المشاكلة (resemblance)
جواهر النفوس (soul substances)

Misconception: Similarity in qualities between two souls means they are identical in essence.
Correction: The fourth group argues that resemblance in qualities does not indicate likeness in quiddity; each soul has a unique essence regardless of shared qualities.

The Argument for Souls Being Identical in Essence (Tamathul)
Razi presents the proof for tamathul via a dilemma based on shared concept and simplicity of souls.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the claim that human rational souls are identical in their complete quiddity (tamathul), and how the argument uses the simplicity of souls to reject any difference in essence.

Core Idea
If souls differed in any way, they would be composite; but souls are simple substances, so they are identical in essence.

This passage presents the key argument used by those who affirm that human rational souls are not merely similar but identical in their essential nature. The argument proceeds from a shared premise and a dilemma, concluding that any supposed difference would contradict the simplicity of the soul. As you read, notice how the argument forces the conclusion that any variation must come from external factors like temperament, not from the soul itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Pay attention to the logical structure: premise, dilemma, rejection of one option, conclusion.
The argument is concise; each step matters.
2
Identify the shared premise
What do all rational human souls share according to the argument? Find the phrase that states this equality.
It is the basis for the dilemma.
3
Understand the dilemma
The argument presents two possibilities: either souls differ in some respect or they do not. Why is the first option rejected?
Focus on the reason given: composition is impossible for simple substances.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the first option is impossible, the second must hold. What is the conclusion about the essence of souls? And what does the last sentence say about differences in actions?
The conclusion is that souls are identical in complete quiddity; differences are due to temperament.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القائلون بتماثل النفوس في تمام الماهية. فقد احتجوا على صحة قولهم : بأن قالوا : لا شك أن النفوس الناطقة متساوية في كونها نفوساً ناطقة بشرية . وبعد حصول الاستواء في هذا المفهوم. إما أن يقال : إنها مختلفة باعتبار آخر ، وإما أن لا تكون كذلك . والأول باطل . وإلا لكان ما به المشاركة غير ما به المخالفة ، فحينئذ يلزم كون كل واحدة من تلك النفوس مركبة من جزءين ، وذلك على النفوس التي هي [ جواهر (٣) ] مجردة : محال . ولما بطل هذا القسم ، بقي الثاني . وهو أن النفوس الناطقة البشرية ، كما أنها متساوية في هذا المعنى ، فهي متساوية في تمام الماهية . وأفعالها على اختلاف الأمزجة.
As for those who affirm the similarity of souls in complete quiddity, they argued for the correctness of their statement by saying: There is no doubt that rational souls are equal in being rational human souls. After establishing equality in this concept, either it is said that they differ in another respect, or they are not so. The first is false, because then that by which they participate would be different from that by which they differ, and then it would follow that each of those souls is composed of two parts, and that for souls which are simple substances is impossible. Since this division is false, the second remains: that rational human souls, just as they are equal in this meaning, are equal in complete quiddity. And their actions [differ] according to different temperaments.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the doctrine that souls are similar (tamathul) in complete quiddity. The argument starts from a shared premise: rational human souls are all equal in being rational human souls – they share a common concept. The proponent then poses a dilemma: if they differ in some additional respect, then they must have a part by which they share and a part by which they differ, which would make them composite. But rational souls are simple substances (jawahir mujarrada), so composition is impossible. Therefore, they cannot differ in any respect; they must be identical in complete quiddity. The last sentence notes that any differences in their actions are due to differences in temperaments, not in essence.

Key Terms
التماثل
تمام الماهية
الجواهر المجردة
المزاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the proof denies any difference among souls whatsoever, including in actions or experiences.
Correction: The argument only denies differences in complete quiddity (essence); it allows differences in actions due to temperament, as the last sentence indicates.

Checkpoint
Why does the argument for tamathul claim that souls cannot differ in any respect?
A) Because any difference would make them composite, impossible for simple substances
B) Because the Prophet said souls are like conscripted soldiers
C) Because they share the same temperament
D) Because they are created by the same planetary spirit

Key Takeaway
The argument for tamathul shows that any essential difference among souls would imply composition, which contradicts the nature of simple substances; thus souls are identical in essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all human souls are identical in essence, then no one has a 'better' soul by birth. What does that mean for how you view people who are less fortunate or who make mistakes? Can you still look down on them, knowing that their soul is just like yours? This lesson reveals that differences in actions stem from temperament, not from a difference in the soul itself. How will you change your attitude towards others, especially those you are quick to judge, starting today?
?
Since your actions are influenced by your temperament and not by any essential superiority of your soul, are you willing to take full responsibility for your actions? Or do you sometimes excuse your bad habits by saying 'that's just how I am'? This lesson teaches that the soul is pure, but your temperament can lead to wrong actions. What specific temperamental trait do you need to work on to align your actions with the purity of your soul?
?
The argument shows that you are no different in essence from anyone else. Does that thought humble you or make you uncomfortable? How does this affect your pride or your sense of self-worth? Reflect on a time when you felt superior to someone else; now realize that your soul is identical. How can you use this truth to cultivate genuine humility and empathy?

Argument for the Essential Identity of Human Souls
Author presents the argument that all rational souls are identical in essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument used to support the claim that all human rational souls are identical in essence (tamathul fi tamam al-mahiyya), and why the author considers this the best reconstruction of that view.

Core Idea
If souls differed in essence, they would be composite—impossible for incorporeal beings.

This passage presents a key argument from those who affirm the essential similarity (tamathul) of all human souls. The reasoning is subtle but powerful: it tries to show that any difference between souls beyond their shared nature would make them composite, which is impossible for simple, incorporeal substances. The author reconstructs this argument carefully, noting that he has no explicit text from earlier authorities to rely on.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument come through.
Pay attention to the logical connectors like 'فإما أن يقال' and 'والأول باطل'.
2
Identify the two alternatives
The argument presents two possibilities after establishing that all rational souls share the concept 'human rational soul'. Find these two alternatives and notice how the first is rejected.
3
Understand the rejection of the first alternative
The author argues that if souls differed in some other respect, they would be composed of what they share and what differs. Why is composition impossible for incorporeal substances? Reflect on this.
This step is crucial: it hinges on the simplicity of incorporeal souls.
4
Grasp the conclusion and its implication
With the first alternative invalidated, the second remains: souls are equal in complete essence. Then note how the author explains differences in perceptions as due to bodily temperaments.
The conclusion is that any variation in perceptions is external, not essential.
5
Note the author's remark
The author admits this is his reconstruction, as he found no explicit statement from 'the Shaykh' on this matter. Consider why this remark is important.
It shows the author is carefully representing the view, not necessarily endorsing it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القائلون بتماثل النفوس في تمام الماهية. فقد احتجوا على صحة قولهم : بأن قالوا : لا شك أن النفوس الناطقة متساوية في كونها نفوساً ناطقة بشرية . وبعد حصول الاستواء في هذا المفهوم. إما أن يقال : إنها مختلفة باعتبار آخر ، وإما أن لا تكون كذلك . والأول باطل . وإلا لكان ما به المشاركة غير ما به المخالفة ، فحينئذ يلزم كون كل واحدة من تلك النفوس مركبة من جزءين ، وذلك على النفوس التي هي جواهر مجردة : محال . ولما بطل هذا القسم ، بقي الثاني . وهو أن النفوس الناطقة البشرية ، كما أنها متساوية في هذا المعنى ، فهي متساوية في تمام الماهية . وأفعالها وإذا ثبت هذا ، فحينئذ يجب أن يكون مجال اختلاف النفوس في إدراكاتها ، على اختلاف الأمزجة. هذا هو الوجه الذي تكلفناه للقوم . وإن كنا ما رأينا للشيخ البتة، في هذا الباب : كلاماً .
As for those who affirm the similarity of souls in the complete essence, they have argued for the correctness of their claim by saying: There is no doubt that rational souls are equal in being human rational souls. After equality in this concept is established, either it is said that they differ in some other respect, or that they are not like that. The first is false, for otherwise what they share would be different from what they differ in, and then it would follow that each one of those souls is composed of two parts, and that is impossible for souls that are incorporeal substances. When this alternative is invalidated, the second remains, namely that rational human souls, just as they are equal in this meaning, are equal in the complete essence. And their actions. And if this is established, then necessarily the field of difference in souls' perceptions must be according to differences in temperaments. This is the way we have gone to trouble for the people, even though we have not seen from the Shaykh any speech at all on this chapter.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents the argument for the view that all human rational souls are identical in essence (tamathul fi tamam al-mahiyya). The author first states the argument: since all rational souls share the concept of being rational human souls, and if they differed in something else besides this concept, they would be composite, which is impossible for incorporeal substances; therefore they must be identical in essence. Then he adds that their actions (af'aluha) are also similar, and any differences in perceptions are due to external factors like bodily temperaments (amzija). Finally, the author notes that this is the best reconstruction he can offer for this view, as he has no explicit statement from the shaykh (likely Ibn Sina or another authority) on this matter. The passage thus sets up the argument that will be critically examined in the following objections.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamathul)
نفوس ناطقة (nufus natiqa)
ماهية (mahiyya)
جواهر مجردة (jawahir mujarrada)
أمزجة (amzija)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Souls can be essentially different without being composite.
Correction: For incorporeal substances like souls, any real difference beyond the shared concept would imply composition into shared and differing parts, which is impossible for simples. Therefore souls must be identical in essence.

Checkpoint
What is the core premise of the argument for tamathul of souls?
A) Souls are composed of two parts.
B) If souls differed in essence, they would be composite, which is impossible for incorporeal substances.
C) Souls are identical in their perceptions.
D) Souls are corporeal.

Key Takeaway
The argument for tamathul relies on the principle that incorporeal souls cannot be composite, so any perceived difference must come from external factors like temperaments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel superior to someone else because of your intelligence or spiritual insight, what does this argument reveal about the source of that superiority? Could it be merely your bodily temperament? How does that change your view of yourself? Are you willing to let go of pride based on something not truly your own?
?
If all human souls are identical in essence, then what truly distinguishes a person's worth in your eyes? Do you treat some people as inherently lesser because of their intellectual or moral failings? Examine your daily interactions: where do you need to recognize the essential equality of souls?
?
The argument says differences in perception are due to temperaments. Is your soul's potential for knowledge and virtue limited by your physical makeup, or can you transcend it through discipline? Honestly reflect: do you use your temperament as an excuse for laziness or sin, or do you actively strive to purify your soul beyond its bodily constraints?

The First Objection: Shared Functions Do Not Prove Identical Essences
First objection: shared effects do not necessitate identical essences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sharing functions like governance and knowledge does not prove that souls are identical in essence.

Core Idea
Simple essences can differ in nature while sharing the same effects.

The pro-tamathul argument attempts to prove that all human souls are identical because they share the functions of governing the body and being rational. However, the first objection challenges this inference by pointing out that shared effects do not require shared essences. Before we examine the rebuttals, let us understand how the objection dismantles the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that the objection begins by defining what 'being a soul' and 'being rational' mean in terms of functions.
Look for the distinction between essence (dhat) and effects (athar).
2
Identify the two key definitions
The objection defines 'soul' as a governor of the body and 'rational' as capable of universal sciences. Observe how these are functional, not essential, definitions.
These definitions are shared by all souls, which the pro-argument uses to claim identity.
3
Understand the refutation principle
The objection states that it is rationally possible for simple essences (māhiyyāt basīṭa) that differ in their specific natures to share some effects and concomitants. This undermines the inference from shared effects to identical essences.
Simple essences are non-composite; their differences are intrinsic, not merely functional.
4
Conclude the lesson
Thus, the first objection successfully shows that the pro-argument's inference is weak. The shared functions of governance and knowledge do not force us to conclude that all souls are identical in essence.
This objection sets the stage for further discussion in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن هذه الحجة ضعيفة جداً من وجوه : الأول : إن المراد من كونها نفوساً : كونها مديرة لهذه الأبدان . والمراد من كونها ناطقة : كونها قابلة للعلوم الكلية ، والإدراكات المجردة العقلية . وهذا يقتضي اشتراك هذه النفوس في كونها مديرة للأبدان وفي كونها قابلة للعلوم . وقد ثبت : أنه لا يمتنع في العقول أن تكون الماهيات البسيطة المختلفة بحسب ذواتها المخصوصة ، تكون متساوية في بعض الآثار واللوازم . وعلى هذا التقدير فقد سقطت هذه الحجة
Know that this argument is very weak from several aspects. First: The meaning of 'being souls' is that they are governors of these bodies, and the meaning of 'being rational' is that they are capable of universal sciences and abstract intellectual perceptions. This necessitates that these souls share in being governors of bodies and being capable of sciences. And it is established that it is not impossible in reason that simple essences that differ according to their specific natures be equal in some effects and concomitants. On this assumption, this argument falls.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection (السؤال الأول) against the argument for tamathul. The objection distinguishes the functional definitions of 'soul' (as governor of the body) and 'rational' (as capable of universal sciences). The pro-tamathul argument claims that sharing these functions implies sharing in essence. The objection refutes this by stating that simple essences (māhiyyāt basīṭa) can be different in their specific natures (dhawātihā al-makhṣūṣa) yet still share some effects (āthār) and necessary concomitants (lawāzim). Therefore, sharing the functions of governance and knowledge does not prove identity of essence. Thus the first objection nullifies the proof.

Key Terms
حجة (hujja)
سؤال الأول (su'al al-awwal)
مدير الأبدان (mudir al-abdan)
قابل للعلوم الكلية (qabil lil-ulum al-kulliyya)
ماهيات بسيطة (māhiyyāt basīṭa)
آثار ولوازم (athar wa lawazim)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sharing any attributes implies sharing in essence.
Correction: Simple essences can differ in specific nature while sharing effects and concomitants.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the first objection?
A) Souls are not governors of bodies.
B) Simple essences can differ in nature while sharing some effects.
C) The argument is strong.
D) Souls are corporeal.

Key Takeaway
Sharing functional attributes does not necessitate identity of essence, because simple essences can differ in nature while sharing some effects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objection shows that sharing the same functions (like rationality and governance of the body) does not prove identical essences. In your own life, do you ever assume that because someone performs the same religious acts as you, their inner state of faith is the same? How might this misconception affect your judgment of others, and what should you check in yourself instead?
?
This passage distinguishes between a soul's specific nature and its effects. Reflect on your own soul: are you focused more on the 'effects' of your actions (outward results) or on the 'specific nature' of your intention and connection with Allah? Which one is more important in the sight of Allah? What changes can you make today to align your soul's inner nature with what pleases Him?
?
The argument that shared functions prove identical essences is weak. Similarly, we might think that similar outward worship proves identical closeness to Allah. How can you personally avoid falling into this assumption and instead work on the unique essence of your faith before Allah?

Second Objection: Attributes Are Acquired, Not Essential
The second objection argues that governance and knowledge are external attributes acquired after essence completion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that governance and knowledge are external attributes acquired after the essence is complete, and thus sharing them does not imply sharing in essence.

Core Idea
Attributes like governance and knowledge are acquired, not essential; they don't prove essence-sharing.

The opponent now raises a second objection against the argument from tamathul (similarity). The objection argues that the attributes of being a governor and having knowledge are not part of the soul's essence but are acquired after the essence is complete. Therefore, sharing these attributes between souls does not entail that they share in their essential nature. This distinction between essential and accidental attributes is crucial in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without over-analyzing, then the literal translation. Get a feel for the objection's flow.
The passage is a self-contained argument.
2
Identify the logical structure
Break down the objection into its core claim, premise, and conclusion. Note how the premise (attributes come after essence completion) leads to the conclusion (attributes are external, so sharing doesn't affect essence).
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this matters: it defends the possibility that souls can have similar capacities yet be essentially different. This is a key counter-argument to the tamathul proof.
Think about how this relates to the broader debate on the nature of the soul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الثاني : إن كونها مديرة للأبدان ، وكونها قادرة على تدبير الأبدان : أحكام. إنما تحصل بعد تمام الماهية ، لأنه ما لم تتم ذاته ، امتنع أن يصير موصوفاً بالقدرة على تدبير الأبدان ، وامتنع أن يصير موصوفاً بكونه قابلاً للعلوم الكلية ، والمعارف القدسية. فثبت بهذا البرهان : أن هذه المعاني : أمور خارجة عن الماهية ، وغير مقومة لها ، ولا داخلة فيها . وإذا كان كذلك ، لم يلزم من وقوع المشاركة فيها حصول المشاركة في جزء من الأجزاء المقومة للماهية .
The second question: That they are governors of bodies and that they are capable of governing bodies are judgments. They are only obtained after the completion of the essence, because as long as its essence is not complete, it is impossible that it become described as capable of governing bodies, and impossible that it become described as being capable of universal sciences and holy knowledges. So it is proven by this demonstration that these meanings are matters external to the essence, not constituting it, and not entering into it. And if such is the case, then from the occurrence of sharing in them does not follow obtaining sharing in any part of the parts that constitute the essence.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is the second objection (السؤال الثاني) against the tamathul argument. It argues that the attributes of being a governor of bodies and being capable of knowledge are not part of the essence itself but are acquired after the essence is complete. The objection employs a demonstration (burhān): since the essence must be complete before it can be described with these attributes, the attributes are external to the essence (khārija ‘an al-māhiyya) and non-constitutive (ghayr muqawwima). Therefore, sharing in these attributes does not entail sharing in any constituent part of the essence. Thus even if souls share the capacity to govern and know, they may still differ in essence.

Key Terms
أحكام (ahkam)
تمام الماهية (tamam al-mahiyya)
خارج عن الماهية (kharij 'an al-mahiyya)
مقوم (muqawwim)
مشاركة (musharaka)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two things share an attribute (like governance), they must share the same essence.
Correction: The objection argues that such attributes are acquired after essence completion and are external to the essence, so sharing them does not imply sharing in the essence itself.

Checkpoint
According to the second objection, why does sharing in governance and knowledge not imply sharing in essence?
A) Because these attributes are essential.
B) Because these attributes are external to the essence and acquired after its completion.
C) Because souls are composite.
D) Because governance is not real.

Key Takeaway
Governance and knowledge are external attributes that do not affect the essence, so sharing them does not prove essential unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered that your most impressive abilities (knowledge, leadership) are actually external to who you really are? How might that change what you value about yourself?
?
If sharing in governance and knowledge does not prove essential unity, what are the implications for how you view your relationship with God? Do you sometimes rely on shared attributes to feel close to Him, rather than focusing on the essence of faith?
?
The objection says that attributes come after essence is complete. Think of an attribute you acquired later in life (a skill, a title). Does defining yourself by it feel more unstable now? What would it mean to live from your essence rather than from what you have?

Two Types of Causes for Differences in Souls
Classifies causes of soul differences into essential and external, enumerating four external causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that differences in human souls and their attributes are caused by both an intrinsic essential factor and a set of four external influences.

Core Idea
Soul differences stem from both inner essence and outer environment.

In this passage, the author provides a clear framework for understanding why human souls and their attributes differ. He divides the causes into two fundamental types: one that is inherent in the soul's own essence, and another that comes from external factors. This classification helps us see that human diversity is not accidental but follows a structured pattern.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Pay attention to the structure and key terms.
Notice how the author uses 'اعلم' to command attention.
2
Identify the two main types
Find the two types of causes: the essential intrinsic cause and the external matters. Understand that both contribute to differences in souls.
3
List the four external causes
From the second type, enumerate the four external causes: ascendants, planets, the six causes (including breastfeeding), and temperaments of limbs.
Each cause is described with a condition that affects the outcome.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the author includes both intrinsic and extrinsic factors. This shows a comprehensive view of human diversity.
This connects to the broader Islamic theological discussion of free will and destiny.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني في ذكر جملة الأسباب الموجبة لاختلاف النفوس في الصفات. اعلم : أنها على نوعين : أحدها: السبب الذاتي الجوهري، وهو الذي ذكرناه من أن النفوس تكون مختلفة في الماهيات والذوات. والنوع الثاني : الأمور الخارجة عن الذات والجوهر ، وهي أربعة أمور : الأول : اختلاف طوالع مسقط الماء وظهور الطوالع . والثاني : اختلاف أحوال الكواكب المسامتة لتلك البلدة والتربة . فإن البلدة التي يمر على سمت رؤوس أهلها : كوكب سعد ، تكون أحوالهم حسنة فاضلة ، والتي يمر على سمت رؤوسهم كوكب نحس تكون أحوالهم ملمومة . الثالث : اختلاف أحوال الأسباب السنة الموجودة في تلك البلدة ، ومن جملتها كيفية حال الرضاع . والرابع : اختلاف أمزجة الأعضاء، واختلاف أحوال الأعضاء الآلية في هيأتها وتركيباتها يوجب اختلاف أحوال الصفات والأفعال.
The second chapter on mentioning the sum of the causes necessitating the difference of souls in attributes. Know: that they are of two types: one is the essential intrinsic cause, which we have mentioned, that souls are different in essences and substances. The second type is matters external to essence and substance, and they are four matters: first: the difference of the ascendants of the place of conception and the appearance of the ascendants. Second: the difference of the states of the planets coinciding with that town and its soil. For the town over whose people’s zenith passes a fortunate planet, their states are good and virtuous, and the one over whose zenith passes an unfortunate planet, their states are troubled. Third: the difference of the states of the six causes present in that town, among which is the condition of breastfeeding. Fourth: the difference of the temperaments of the limbs, and the difference of the states of the instrumental limbs in their form and composition necessitates difference in the states of attributes and actions.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage classifies the causes of differences among human souls in their attributes into two fundamental types. The first is the intrinsic essential cause (al-sabab al-dhātī al-jawharī), which the author states he has already mentioned: that souls differ in their very essences and substances (al-māhiyyāt wa al-dhawāt). The second type comprises matters external to essence and substance (al-umūr al-khārija ‘an al-dhāt wa al-jawhar). The author then enumerates four such external causes. The first is the difference in the ascendants (ṭawāli‘) at the time of conception and the appearance of those ascendants. The second is the difference in the states of the planets that are in conjunction with (musāmata) a particular town and its soil; he specifies that fortunate planets bring good qualities and unfortunate planets bring troubled qualities. The third is the difference in the six causes (al-asbāb al-sittah) present in that town, including the condition of breastfeeding. The fourth is the difference in the temperaments (amzijah) of the limbs, and the difference in the states of the instrumental limbs (al-a‘ḍā’ al-āliyyah) in their form and composition, which necessitates differences in the states of attributes and actions. The passage thus establishes a framework for understanding human diversity as resulting from both innate essence and external influences.

Key Terms
السبب الذاتي الجوهري
الأمور الخارجة عن الذات والجوهر
الطوالع
الكواكب
الأسباب السنة
أمزجة الأعضاء
الأعضاء الآلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All soul differences are due to external factors like upbringing or environment.
Correction: The passage affirms a fundamental intrinsic cause: souls differ in their very essences, not just due to external influences.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many external causes are mentioned for differences in souls?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Differences in souls arise from both an inherent essential nature and external factors, with four specific external causes identified.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage lists four external causes for differences in souls. Think of one trait you have that you dislike. Which of these four causes might have contributed to it? How does this understanding affect your gratitude or complaint to Allah?

?
The author includes breastfeeding among the six causes. If you are or plan to be a parent, how does this passage challenge you to take responsibility for the external factors you provide for your child’s soul? What concrete steps can you take?

Galen on Mutual Influence of Soul and Body
Galen presents empirical evidence for reciprocal soul-body interaction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Galen's empirical argument for the mutual influence between the soul and the body.

Core Idea
Body and soul shape each other in a two-way exchange.

Galen, the renowned physician, provides a concrete example from human temperament to argue that the soul and body are not isolated. In his commentary on Hippocrates, he shows that a bilious temperament causes anger, and anger itself increases bile. This passage invites us to see the reciprocal relationship between our physical makeup and our emotional states.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the argument unfold naturally.
Notice the structure: claim, interpretation, conclusion.
2
Identify the two directions of influence
Find where the passage shows body affecting soul (temperament → anger) and soul affecting body (anger → bile accumulation).
These two directions are the core of the mutual influence.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this mutual influence matters for understanding human nature and for theological discussions about the soul-body relationship.
Galen uses empirical observation, not abstract reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال جالينوس في تفسيره لكتاب بقراط في الأخلاط : إن فعل مزاج الأخلاط في النفس مساوي لفعل اختلاف النفس وتفسيره : إن من كان الغالب عليه هو المزاج الصفراوي فإنه يغضب كثيراً وأيضاً إذا غضب مراراً كثيرة غضباً شديداً فإنه يجتمع في بدنه شيئاً كثيراً من الصفراء وهذا يدل على أن النفس والبدن كل واحد منهما مؤثر في الآخر.
Galen said in his commentary on Hippocrates' book on the humors: The effect of the mixture of humors on the soul is equal to the effect of difference of the soul. Its interpretation: Whoever is dominated by the bilious temperament becomes angry often, and also if he becomes angry many times with intense anger, a great amount of bile collects in his body. And this indicates that the soul and the body, each one of them influences the other.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from Galen for the mutual influence between soul and body. Galen, in his commentary on Hippocrates' book on humors, states that the action (fi‘l) of the mixture of humors (mizāj al-akhlāṭ) upon the soul is equal to the action of the soul's own variation. The author then provides an interpretation (tafsīr): a person dominated by the bilious temperament (al-mizāj al-ṣafrāwī) tends to become angry frequently. Conversely, if such a person repeatedly experiences intense anger, a large amount of bile accumulates in his body. This reciprocal relationship demonstrates that the soul (al-nafs) and the body (al-badan) each influence the other. The argument is empirical: physiological temperament affects emotional states, and emotional states in turn cause physiological changes.

Key Terms
جالينوس
بقراط
الأخلاط
المزاج الصفراوي
النفس
البدن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Influence between soul and body is one-way (body affects soul only).
Correction: The passage demonstrates a two-way interaction: body affects soul (temperament causes anger) and soul affects body (anger causes bile accumulation).

Checkpoint
What does Galen's example of bilious temperament prove, according to this passage?
A) The soul has no effect on the body
B) The body and soul influence each other
C) Anger is entirely physiological
D) Bile causes anger only

Key Takeaway
Galen's example of bilious temperament and anger shows that soul and body mutually influence each other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever noticed how your physical state—like tiredness, hunger, or illness—affects your patience or anger? How does Galen's observation challenge you to take more responsibility for your body's condition as part of your spiritual state? What one specific change can you make this week to align your physical habits with your desire for a better soul?
?
The passage says soul and body influence each other equally. In your life, do you tend to neglect your body or your soul? Which one have you been ignoring, and what is one concrete step you can take today to restore balance?
?
When you feel angry, do you consider that your anger might be caused by a physical imbalance? How might remembering this two-way influence change your response the next time you feel anger rising? Commit to one action you will take when you feel anger to address both body and soul.
